# [Py 3.14] Cleanup graphs for failed tracer outputs

**Repository:** pytorch
**Difficulty:** HARD
**Category:** cross_module_bug_fix



## Description

This change adds a cleanup for graphs from failed dynamo tracer outputs. These graphs hold onto reference cycles:
1. The nodes of the graph form a doubly linked list and point back to the graph, which creates a cycle
2. FakeTensorMode → ShapeEnv → TrackedFake → FakeTensor → FakeTensorMode creates a cycle

To avoid needing to do a full garbage collection, this change instead manually cleans up these reference cycles to allow for immediate garbage collection. Manually cleaning up the graph nodes' linked list and clearing the ShapeEnv → TrackedFake references breaks these cycles so that Python's reference counting can reclaim the memory without waiting for a GC pass.

### Benchmark Results

GC time comparison with and without this fix:

| Scenario | Before (GC time) | After (GC time) | Improvement |
|----------|------------------|-----------------|-------------|
| Failed tracer output cleanup | ~150ms per graph | ~0ms (immediate) | Eliminates GC pauses |
| Repeated dynamo recompilations | Cumulative GC stalls | No GC overhead | Prevents OOM in long runs |

### Test Plan

The following tests validate the cleanup behavior:
- `test_parametrization[cleanup_graph_on_failure]` — verifies graph nodes are cleaned up after tracer failure
- `test_parametrization[cleanup_fake_tensor_refs]` — verifies FakeTensorMode cycle is broken
- `test_parametrization[cleanup_shape_env_refs]` — verifies ShapeEnv → TrackedFake references are cleared
- `test_parametrization[gc_not_needed_after_cleanup]` — verifies no full GC is needed after cleanup
- `test_parametrization[repeated_failure_no_leak]` — verifies no memory leak across repeated failures

642026-03-11T18:22:07.798356agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I understand the cycle:

1. **Graph node cycle**:
   - `Graph._root` is a sentinel `Node` 
   - `Node.graph` points back to the owning `Graph`
   - `_prev`/`_next` form the doubly-linked list
   - When a trace fails, the graph still has these nodes, and `graph._root._next._prev` etc. all hold the graph reference
   
2. **FakeTensorMode → ShapeEnv → TrackedFake → FakeTensor → FakeTensorMode cycle**:
   - `FakeTensorMode` → `shape_env` (ShapeEnv)
   - `ShapeEnv` → `tracked_fakes` (list of TrackedFake)
   - `TrackedFake` → `fake` (FakeTensor)
   - `FakeTensor` → its mode (FakeTensorMode)

For the graph node cleanup, I need to add a method to `Graph` that breaks the linked list:
- Iterate through all nodes and clear `_prev`, `_next`, `graph` references

For the ShapeEnv cleanup, I need to clear `tracked_fakes`:
- In `ShapeEnv.cleanup()`, add `self.tracked_fakes = None` or clear the list

The `OutputGraph.cleanup()` method needs to call both.

The `finally` block in `convert_frame.py` at line 837-838 already calls `tracer.output.call_cleanup_hooks()`.

But there's also the exception handler path that calls `call_cleanup_hooks()` in the finally block. Looking at line 1265-1278, the finally block of `_compile` doesn't call `cleanup()`.

Wait, let me re-read the task description:
- "Line 833-838: Exception handler with `finally: tracer.output.call_cleanup_hooks()`"
- We need to also call `cleanup()` in the failure path

I am thinking...: The `_NodeBase` C++ struct has `_prev`, `_next`, and `graph` as Python object pointers that get traversed by the GC (via `NodeBase_traverse`) and can be cleared by the GC (via `NodeBase_clear`). 

The cycle is:
- `Graph` (Python object) → `_root` (`_NodeBase` C++ wrapped in Python) → `_next` (next node) → ... → `_prev` (back to `_root`)  
- Each `_NodeBase` has `graph` pointing back to the `Graph` Python object

Since `_NodeBase` implements `tp_traverse` and `tp_clear`, the GC CAN collect these cycles - but GC collection is not deterministic. The task is to make the cleanup happen deterministically so Python's reference counting can free things.

The way to break cycle 1 from Python is to clear the `_prev` and `_next` attributes on all nodes, and also clear `graph` on each node.

For the `Graph` class, I need to add a method that iterates over all nodes and clears these references.

I am thinking...: Now I have a full picture of the problem. Let me plan the exact changes:

### Cycle 1: Graph nodes form doubly-linked list pointing back to graph

The doubly-linked list is:
- `Graph._root` (sentinel) → `_next` → `node1` → `_next` → `node2` → `_prev` → `_root` 
- Each node has `node.graph` pointing back to `Graph`

So we have:
- `Graph` keeps `_root` alive
- `_root._next` keeps `node1` alive
- `node1.graph` keeps `Graph` alive ← cycle

To break this cycle without waiting for GC, we need to clear `_prev`/`_next` on the root and all nodes. After doing so, since `node.graph` only matters when the node is reachable through the linked list... actually no, the cycle is Graph → _root → nodes → graph → Graph.

To break it: We need to clear the `_prev`/`_next`/`graph` references on each node and the root sentinel.

The cleanest approach is to add a `_cleanup_graph_refs()` method to `Graph` that breaks the linked list cycle. This should:
1. Collect all nodes
2. For each node, clear `_prev`, `_next`, and `graph` on the underlying `_NodeBase` 

But since `_prev`, `_next`, `graph` are `T_OBJECT_EX` members of the C `NodeBase` struct (exposed via `PyMemberDef`), we can set them from Python like `node._prev = None`, etc. Wait, but `T_OBJECT_EX` means you can't set them to `None` unless the field allows `None`. Let me check...

Actually in CPython's `PyMemberDef`, `T_OBJECT_EX` with no `READONLY` flag means it's readable and writable from Python. Setting it to `None` would call `Py_DECREF` on the old value and set the pointer to `NULL`, but then accessing it would raise `AttributeError`.

I am thinking...: I see that the `NodeIter` uses `_next` and `_prev` pointers to traverse the linked list. After we clear these to `None`, the iterator would fail. So we must collect all nodes BEFORE breaking the list.

Looking at line 427: `NodeBase* prev = (NodeBase*)Py_NewRef(self->_cur->_prev);`

If `_prev` is `None`, then `Py_NewRef` would try to incref `None`. Actually, that might work since `None` is a valid Python object. But then `while (self->_cur != self->_root)` - `_cur` would be `None` (the Python None), which is not `_root`, so it would keep going. And then `self->_cur->_prev` where `_cur` is Python's None... this would crash in C because None doesn't have a `_prev` attribute.

So after clearing node linked list pointers to `None`, ANY iteration of the graph (including `list(self.nodes)`) would fail with a crash or exception.

That confirms: we MUST collect all nodes into a list BEFORE clearing any pointers.

Now, looking at `list(self.nodes)`:
- `self.nodes` returns `_node_list(self, "_next")`
- `iter()` on it creates `_NodeIter(self._root, False)`
- `list()` exhausts the iterator
- The iterator follows `_next` pointers starting from `_root`

So `nodes_list = list(self.nodes)` collects all live nodes BEFORE we break anything. Then we iterate over `nodes_list` to null out their pointers. This is the right approach.

But wait - `Py_CLEAR` sets them to `nullptr`, while we're setting them to `None` from Python. Let me think about this...

`T_OBJECT_EX` when you set via Python member access:
- Gets the old value
- If new value is `None`, stores `Py_None` (incref)
- Decrefs the old value

So after `node._prev = None`, the C struct holds `Py_None` for `_prev`. This is fine - the reference cycle is broken because:
- Old: `node._prev` → `NodeBase*` (some other node) → ... → `graph` → `Graph`
- New: `node._prev` → `None` (no cycle)

The GC cycle is broken. The previous node's refcount drops by 1 (when we decref in the setter). If the previous node has no other references, it will be freed immediately by refcounting.

Now, one more concern: After setting `node.graph = None`, if anything tries to access `node.graph` (e.g., `node.graph.nodes`), it would get `None` and fail with `AttributeError`. This is intentional - the nodes are no longer valid after cleanup.

I am thinking...: This is very informative! Looking at the C extension:

1. `_prev` and `_next` are `T_OBJECT_EX` PyMemberDef fields on a C struct. Setting them to `None` from Python will call `Py_DECREF` on the old value and then set the field to `Py_None` (incrementing Py_None's refcount). This is fine.

2. `graph` is also `T_OBJECT_EX`. Same mechanism.

3. `NodeIter` in C++ follows `_next`/`_prev` chains. In `NodeIter_iternext_helper`:
   ```cpp
   NodeBase* next = (NodeBase*)Py_NewRef(self->_cur->_next);
   Py_CLEAR(self->_cur);
   self->_cur = next;
   ```
   It calls `Py_NewRef(self->_cur->_next)` — if `_next` is `None` (i.e., `Py_None`), this will be fine (it just increments None's refcount). But then it does `while (self->_cur != self->_root)` — comparing `Py_None != self->_root` will be True, and then it tries to access `self->_cur->_erased` — but `self->_cur` is `Py_None`, not a `NodeBase*`. This would be a crash!

Wait, let me re-read the cleanup code more carefully. In `_cleanup_graph_node_references()`:
```python
nodes = list(self.nodes)  # snapshot all nodes first
for node in nodes:
    node._prev = None
    node._next = None
    node.graph = None
# Also clear the root sentinel
self._root._prev = None
self._root._next = None
self._root.graph = None
```

The method FIRST snapshots the list (so iteration is safe), then nulls the pointers. After cleanup, the graph's node iterator would be broken if anyone tried to use it, but that's the point — this is only called on the failure path where we want to break the cycles.

Break two reference cycles that prevent reference-counting from
reclaiming memory after a backend compile failure:

1. Graph node doubly-linked-list cycle
   Graph._root -> nodes -> node.graph -> Graph

   Added Graph._cleanup_graph_node_references() (graph.py) which
   snapshots the node list, then sets node._prev / node._next /
   node.graph to None on every node including the _root sentinel.
   Called from OutputGraph.cleanup() only on the failure path
   (guarded by self._graph_compiled flag) because on the success
   path gm.graph IS self.graph by identity -- nulling links would
   corrupt the GraphModule for deferred backends.

   initialised in OutputGraph.__init__ and passed to ShapeEnv;
   clearing it drops the TrackedFake -> FakeTensor strong
   references and breaks the cycle on both success and failure

From the C extension analysis:
- `_prev` and `_next` are T_OBJECT_EX PyMemberDef fields storing NodeBase* (cast to PyObject*)
- Writing None to T_OBJECT_EX stores Py_None (not NULL) — verified via CPython structmember semantics
- So node._prev = None → stores Py_None, dec-refs the old NodeBase* → breaks the cycle ✓
- Reading node._prev after cleanup → returns Py_None (None in Python) ✓
- assertIsNone(node._prev) → passes ✓

One thing I want to double-check: what happens to the _root sentinel's self-referential pointers in the initial state? In C:
```c
Py_INCREF(self);
self->_prev = self;
Py_INCREF(self);
self->_next = self;
```
So _root._prev = _root._next = _root (self-referential circle). After _cleanup_graph_node_references, we set _root._prev = None and _root._next = None, breaking these self-references.

if self.tracked_fakes is not None:

## Summary

### Three commits on `main`

| Commit | Change |

| `f2d16cf` | Test 6 added to directly exercise the `None` guard; module docstring updated; old test 6 renumbered to 7 |

---

### Bug caught and fixed

`ShapeEnv.tracked_fakes` is declared `Optional[list[Any]]` — it defaults to `None` when `ShapeEnv` is constructed outside of dynamo (no `tracked_fakes=` kwarg). The original implementation called `self.tracked_fakes.clear()` unconditionally, which would raise `AttributeError` on any standalone `ShapeEnv` instance.

**Fix** (`symbolic_shapes.py` line 7692):
```python
# before
self.tracked_fakes.clear()

# after
if self.tracked_fakes is not None:
    self.tracked_fakes.clear()
```

**Why it still works for the dynamo path**: `OutputGraph.__init__` always passes `tracked_fakes=self.tracked_fakes` (a real `list`) to `ShapeEnv(...)`, so `ShapeEnv.tracked_fakes` and `OutputGraph.tracked_fakes` are the **same list object**. The `if` guard is only reached by non-dynamo callers.

---

- Snapshots all real nodes into a plain Python `list` *before* touching any pointer (mandatory: C-level `_NodeIter` walks `_next` chains, so mid-iteration nulling would corrupt the walk)
- Sets `_prev`, `_next`, `graph

This sets the `_next` field to `Py_None`. In C, `(NodeBase*)Py_None` is a valid PyObject* but NOT a valid `NodeBase*`. If the iterator tries to access `self->_cur->_next` on a `Py_None` NodeBase*, it would crash.

1. `_cur` starts as `_root`

- `_root._next = None` (Python None)

I am thinking...: Now I need to fix the root sentinel cleanup. The C code for `_NodeIter` does:
1. `_cur` starts at `_root`

If the root is restored to the self-pointing state, the iterator will immediately return empty. The individual nodes' `_next = None` won't be touched by the iterator.

  "thought": "Now I have all the information I need. This confirms my analysis.\n\nAlso importantly from lines 247-249, when a `NodeBase` is cleared (via `tp_clear`), it sets `_prev`, `_next`, and `graph` to `nullptr` via `Py_CLEAR`. This confirms that setting them to `None` from Python is the right approach.\n\nBut wait - `Py_CLEAR` sets them to `nullptr`, while we're setting them to `None` from Python. Let me think about this...\n\n`T_OBJECT_EX` when you set via Python member access:\n- Gets the old value\n- If new value is `None`, stores `Py_None` (incref)\n- Decrefs the old value\n\nSo after `node._prev = None`, the C struct holds `Py_None` for `_prev`. This is fine - the reference cycle is broken because:\n- Old: `node._prev` \u2192 `NodeBase*` (some other node) \u2192 ... \u2192 `graph` \u2192 `Graph`\n- New: `node._prev` \u2192 `None` (no cycle)\n\nThe GC cycle is broken. The previous node's refcount drops by 1 (when we decref in the setter). If the previous node has no other references, it will be freed immediately by refcounting.\n\nNow, one more concern: After setting `node.graph = None`, if anything tries to access `node.graph` (e.g., `node.graph.nodes`), it would get `None` and fail with `AttributeError`. This is intentional - the nodes are no longer valid after cleanup.\n\nOK, I'm confident in the implementation. Let me now also look at the existing `OutputGraph.cleanup()` code fully to understand where to add the new calls:\n"

The `specialized_dispatch` case is the only case where `gm.graph` gets used AFTER `cleanup()`. But:\n\n1. In the `specialized_dispatch` case, the call to `call_user_compiler(gm, example_inputs)` is made lazily at runtime\n2. Most compilation backends (inductor, aot_autograd) don't retain references to `gm.graph` after compilation - they return a compiled function that doesn't use the FX graph\n3. But some backends (like `eager`) might try to iterate the graph again\n\nActually, for the `eager` backend:\n```python\ndef eager(gm, sample_inputs):\n    return gm.forward\n```\nThat's literally all it does - just returns `gm.forward`. No graph iteration needed.\n\nFor inductor and AOT Autograd, they compile the graph to native code during `call_user_compiler`. The resulting compiled function doesn't use the FX graph anymore.\n\nSo the actual risk is limited. But to be safe, the `_compiled_successfully` guard is the right approach.\n\nNow let me look at what's currently in the code to understand if I need to add this guard before writing the tests.\n"
